(A minimal increase of mean answer time and mean time for correct answer was observed after 4 h after high dosage intake and 1 h after low dosage intake. – More pronounced after the low dosage.) |  | _H. lupulus_ | 2 |
| 19 | Lindahl O 1989[83](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr83-2515690X20967323) | Randomized, placebo-controlled, double-blind, cross-over<br>Population: Volunteers with sleep difficulties and fatigue. (n=27) | Intervention: Single doses of (1) test preparation: _V. officinalis_ extract (equivalent to 400 mg of the root), _H. lupulus_ extract (375 mg equivalent) and _M. officinalis_ extract (160 mg equivalent) or (2) Control: same amounts of hops and lemon balm and V. officinalis 4 mg equivalent<br>Measures: Subjective rating of sleep quality | 78% rated high valerian preparation better than the control. | No side effects. | _H. lupulus_<br>_M. officinalis_ | 2 |

Abbreviations: BDI-Beck Depression Inventory, DISS-Defined Intensity Stress Simulator, DSST-Digit Symbol Substitution Test, DST-Digit Span Test, EEG-Electroencephalogram, HAM-A-Hamilton Anxiety Rating Scale, ICD-10-International Classification of Diseases 10th Revision, ISI-Insomnia Severity Index, PSQI-Pittsburgh Sleep Quality Index, TSST -, WASO-Wake Time After Sleep Onset

### _V. Officinalis_ as a Single Herb

#### Sleep problems

To evaluate the effectiveness of valerian for sleep problems, 40 articles using _V. officinalis_ as a single herb were assessed. As a result, it was found that 23 studies addressed the effectiveness of valerian for sleep problems. Among them, 13 studies found valerian effective as a sleep aid. Three studies were performed with healthy subjects,[37](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr37-2515690X20967323), [40](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr40-2515690X20967323), [41](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr41-2515690X20967323) 4 studies with insomnia patients,[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [42](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr42-2515690X20967323), [52](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr52-2515690X20967323), [66](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr66-2515690X20967323) and 1 study in RLS patients.[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323) In addition, studies conducted with mental health patients,[67](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr67-2515690X20967323) cancer patients,[56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323) HIV-positive patients,[35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323) postmenopausal women,[57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323) and the elderly,[38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323) also found that valerian could improve sleep quality.[35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323), [56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323), [57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323) On the other hand, 10 studies found that valerian was not significantly effective compared to control[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323), [40](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr40-2515690X20967323), [48](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr48-2515690X20967323), [50](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr50-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323), [53](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr53-2515690X20967323), [54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323), [56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323), [65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323) at least for the outcome measures used in those studies. Study outcomes were assessed using various measures, such as sleep questionnaires and diaries, such as Pittsburgh Sleep Quality Inventory (PSQI),[90](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr90-2515690X20967323) Insomnia Severity Index (ISI),[91](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr91-2515690X20967323) and Epworth Sleepiness Scale (ESS), to polysomnography.[92](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr92-2515690X20967323)

Six studies measured immediate responses after single dose administration,[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323), [40](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr40-2515690X20967323)– [42](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr42-2515690X20967323), [50](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr50-2515690X20967323) while most studies evaluated the effectiveness of repeated doses.[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323), [35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323), [56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323), [57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323), [65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323), [67](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr67-2515690X20967323), [36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323)– [38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323), [44](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr44-2515690X20967323), [48](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr48-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323)– [53](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr53-2515690X20967323) The intervention periods ranged from 5 days to 8 weeks.

In order to extract possible associations between herbal preparations and study outcomes, the reports were classified into 4 groups ( [Table 1](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#table1-2515690X20967323)): 8 studies using hydroalcoholic extracts,[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [42](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr42-2515690X20967323), [44](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr44-2515690X20967323), [50](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr50-2515690X20967323), [52](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr52-2515690X20967323)– [54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323), [65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323) 3 studies using aqueous extracts,[38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323), [40](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr40-2515690X20967323), [41](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr41-2515690X20967323) 3 studies using extracts using unspecified solvents,[37](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr37-2515690X20967323), [48](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr48-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323) and 5 studies using herbal substance (the whole root / rhizome).[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323), [35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323), [57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323), [67](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr67-2515690X20967323) Among the 3 studies using aqueous extracts, 2 studies with single dose found improved subjective sleep quality and latency in healthy volunteers[40](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr40-2515690X20967323), [41](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr41-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 2 and 5\]), while there was no significant difference in polysomnography[40](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr40-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 2\]). Schulz et al. found that repeated administration of _V. officinalis_ aqueous extract (for 1 week) increased deep sleep (slow-wave sleep: SWS) in elderly subjects, although single dose of the same preparation did not have any significant impact on polysomnography[38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 2\]). As a single dose, _V. officinalis_ hydroalcoholic extracts did not improve sleep quality[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [50](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr50-2515690X20967323) (RCT, Jadad scale 2-3), however improved REM sleep was observed in insomnia patients[42](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr42-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 2\]). Repeated administration of hydroalcoholic extracts also led to inconsistent outcomes: sleep quality was improved in 4 studies using extract 600 mg (2 to 6 weeks)[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [37](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr37-2515690X20967323), [44](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr44-2515690X20967323), [52](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr52-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 2-5\]), whereas 3 studies using extract 300-600 mg (5 days to 4 weeks) found no improvement[53](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr53-2515690X20967323), [54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323), [65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 3-5\]). Donath et al. found improved sleep latency and deep sleep after 2 weeks, while no improvement was observed after a single dose[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 2\]), which suggests that repeated administration is needed to exert observable effects. There were 3 studies using extracts with unspecified procedures.[48](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr48-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323), [66](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr66-2515690X20967323) The outcomes from those studies were also inconsistent: negative outcomes for 2 studies[48](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr48-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 5\]) and positive for an observational study.[66](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr66-2515690X20967323) On the other hand, all 5 studies using the dried root/rhizome showed that the interventions led to improved sleep at least in 1 subgroup[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323), [35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323), [57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323), [67](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr67-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad 3-5\] and 1 observational study), suggesting that maximum efficacy could be expected from the root / rhizome before extraction.

It has been suggested that valerian may be useful to improve subjective sleep quality[22](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr22-2515690X20967323) and that repeated administration is required to obtain significant effects.[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323) In order to evaluate if repeated administrations could consistently improve sleep quality, a meta-analysis was carried out ( [Figure 2](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig2-2515690X20967323)). Studies using repeated valerian administrations were assessed to extract numerical values for the meta-analysis, and 10 randomized placebo-controlled trials reporting quantifiable results[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323), [34](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr34-2515690X20967323)– [36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323)– [54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323), [56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323), [57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323) were included in the analysis. The combined effect size was 0.36 (95% CI: -0.08 to 0.81) ( [Figure 2A](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig2-2515690X20967323)). The funnel plot indicated missing data ( [Figure 2B](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig2-2515690X20967323)) and high heterogeneity was observed (I2=85.33%). As described above, differences in herbal preparation could potentially contribute to the heterogenous outcomes. In fact, subgroup analysis for the whole root[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323), [35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [56](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr56-2515690X20967323), [57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad 3-5\]) and the extract[34](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr34-2515690X20967323), [36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323)– [54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad 2-5\]) revealed that the combined effect size for the whole root was considerably higher 0.83 (95% CI: 0.03 to 1.62), compared to the extract (0.10; 95% CI: -0.02 to 0.22) ( [Figure 3](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig3-2515690X20967323)), further supporting the use of the whole root rather than extract.

![](https://journals.sagepub.com/cms/10.1177/2515690X20967323/asset/d399e220-63c7-49ee-96f4-faf3a7b91969/assets/images/large/10.1177_2515690x20967323-fig2.jpg)Figure 2. Sleep quality improvement by repeated administration of _V. officinalis_. Ten studies were included in meta-analysis. Positive values indicate enhanced sleep quality. (A) Forest plot for sleep quality improvement. Effect sizes (Hedges’ g) for 10 studies (blue circles) and combined effect size (green circle) are shown. Black horizontal bars indicate 95% CI. (B) Funnel plot. Included data points are presented as filled blue circles and imputed data are shown as open orange circles.

![](https://journals.sagepub.com/cms/10.1177/2515690X20967323/asset/fa2eff39-9f73-4764-afba-fa3f7f64ab41/assets/images/large/10.1177_2515690x20967323-fig3.jpg)Figure 3. Subgroup analysis for _V. officinalis_ whole root and extract as a sleep aid. Subgroup analysis was performed with 4 studies (1 ∼ 4) using the whole root/rhizome and 6 studies (5 ∼ 10) using extracts. Effect sizes for each group are shown as red circles. Black horizontal bars indicate 95% CI.

#### Anxiety

Anxiety was assessed by Hamilton Anxiety Rating Scale (HAM-A): a clinician-rated scale that considers psychological and somatic factors,[93](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr93-2515690X20967323), [94](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr94-2515690X20967323) State-Trait Anxiety Inventory (STAI): a patient-rated scale that measures state and trait anxiety,[95](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr95-2515690X20967323), [96](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr96-2515690X20967323) mental stress test using the color/word interference task,[97](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr97-2515690X20967323) or other questionnaires. Seven studies examined valerian’s anxiolytic potential, and positive outcomes were observed in 6 studies.[33](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr33-2515690X20967323), [35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [43](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr43-2515690X20967323), [60](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr60-2515690X20967323), [63](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr63-2515690X20967323), [71](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr71-2515690X20967323) Valerian standardized extract 600 mg per day for 1 week reduced psychological and physiological stress reactivity under stress in healthy adult subjects[43](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr43-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 1\]). Average 81.3 mg per day of valepotriates for 4 weeks reduced the score of HAM-A in generalized anxiety disorder patients[71](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr71-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]), suggesting that valepotriates are the active anxiolytic constituents. Valerian root / rhizome 530 mg per day for 4 weeks reduced anxiety in HIV-positive patients receiving efavirenz[35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 3\]), suggesting valerian could prevent neuropsychiatric adverse effects caused by the antiretroviral medication. Valerian extract 100 mg[33](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr33-2515690X20967323) or root / rhizome 100 mg,[60](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr60-2515690X20967323) single dose 60 min before the initiation of surgical operation, reduced anxiety in anxious patients undergoing dental operation[33](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr33-2515690X20967323), [60](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr60-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 5\]). In addition, valerian extract 1,260 mg per day for 7 days for 3 menstrual cycles effectively reduced premenstrual anxiety[63](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr63-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]). However, an internet-based study with volunteers with non-clinical anxiety and insomnia found no significant difference in STAI compared to placebo[51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]). [Figure 4](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig4-2515690X20967323) shows the result of meta-analysis for valerian’s anxiolytic effects based on 7 randomized placebo-controlled trials that reported quantitative outcomes[34](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr34-2515690X20967323), [35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [47](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr47-2515690X20967323), [49](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr49-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323), [60](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr60-2515690X20967323), [63](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr63-2515690X20967323) ( [Figure 4A](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig4-2515690X20967323)). The funnel plot indicated significant publication bias, missing data in the area of negative outcome, and high heterogeneity (I2=93.13%) ( [Figure 4B](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig4-2515690X20967323)). Subgroup analysis revealed high variability for valerian extracts[34](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr34-2515690X20967323), [47](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr47-2515690X20967323), [49](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr49-2515690X20967323), [51](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr51-2515690X20967323), [63](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr63-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 3-5\]), whereas positive outcomes were observed for the whole root[35](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr35-2515690X20967323), [60](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr60-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 3 and 5\]). However, due to the scarcity of data (2 studies for the whole root), it is difficult to draw a conclusion.

![](https://journals.sagepub.com/cms/10.1177/2515690X20967323/asset/1c75a1d9-9e62-4d38-84c8-72b9b2946e36/assets/images/large/10.1177_2515690x20967323-fig4.jpg)Figure 4. _V. officinalis_ for anxiety. Eight studies were included in meta-analysis. Positive values indicate either reduced anxiety or enhanced calmness. (A) Forest plot for anxiety reduction. Effect sizes (Hedges’ g) for each study (blue circles) and combined effect size (green circle) are shown. (B) Funnel plot. Included data points are presented as filled blue circles. (C) Subgroup analysis for _V. officinalis_ whole root (1 and 2) and extracts (3 ∼ 8).

Two studies investigated the effects of _V. officinalis_ extracts on anxiety-associated brain activities.[31](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr31-2515690X20967323), [34](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr34-2515690X20967323) Single dose of 300 mg extract reduced intracortical facilitation, possibly via GABAA enhancement[31](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr31-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 4\]), and hydroalcoholic extract 300 mg per day for 4 weeks increased frontal brain region alpha coherence, which was correlated with anxiolysis[34](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr34-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]). These findings suggest that _V. officinalis_ could induce immediate as well as long-lasting effects on anxiety-associated brain activities.

#### Other therapeutic effects

In addition to insomnia and anxiety, several other therapeutic benefits were suggested ( [Figure 5](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig5-2515690X20967323)). Valerian aqueous extract 750 mg per day for 8 weeks was effective in reducing the symptoms of obsessive-compulsive disorder (OCD)[55](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr55-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 2\]). Valerian root / rhizome 530 mg per day for 1 month improved cognition in haemodialysis patients[32](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr32-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 2\]), and valerian root / rhizome 1,060 mg per day for 8 weeks prevented cognitive dysfunction after coronary bypass surgery[61](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr61-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]). Valerian root / rhizome 675 mg or extract 1,060 mg per day for 8 weeks reduced severity and frequency of hot flashes in menopausal and postmenopausal women[59](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr59-2515690X20967323), [64](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr64-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 4\]). In addition, valerian root / rhizome 765 mg per day for 3 days for 2 cycles reduced pain severity and syncope in young females with dysmenorrhea[58](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr58-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]), and valerian extract 1,260 mg for 7 days for 3 cycles reduced premenstrual symptoms[63](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr63-2515690X20967323), supporting the traditional use of valerian as a menstrual stimulant.[16](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr16-2515690X20967323)

![](https://journals.sagepub.com/cms/10.1177/2515690X20967323/asset/2d1beef7-2aba-4d66-ab2c-92f61a6deca8/assets/images/large/10.1177_2515690x20967323-fig5.jpg)Figure 5. Valerian’s active constituents and potential therapeutic benefits.

### Other Valerian Species

Three studies investigated the effectiveness of other _Valeriana_ spp. as a sleep aid: 2 studies on _V. edulis_ [42](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr42-2515690X20967323), [46](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr46-2515690X20967323) and 1 study on _V. wallichii_.[70](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr70-2515690X20967323) _V. edulis_ 20 mg/kg for 2 weeks reduced sleep latencies and improved sleep quality in children with intellectual deficit and primary sleep problems[46](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr46-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]), and _V. edulis_ hydroalcoholic extract 450 mg single dose increased REM sleep and reduced the number of awaking in insomnia patients[42](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr42-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]). A concoction of valepotriates from _V. wallichii_ 300 mg per day for 15 days reduced Wake Time After Sleep Onset (WASO) and improved sleep quality in insomnia patients[70](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr70-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 3\]). Of note, chemical characteristics of the 3 species ( _V. officinalis_, _V. edulis_, and _V. wallichi_) significantly differ; valerenic acids (valerenic acid, acetoxyvalerenic acid, hydroxyvalerenic acid) are specific to _V. officin_ a _lis_, whereas valepotriates (valtrate and isovaltrate) are common among the 3 species,[98](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr98-2515690X20967323) suggesting that valepotriates at least in part contribute to valerian’s sleep promoting activity. Due to the scarcity of data, it was not possible to perform meta-analysis for _V. edulis_ and _V. wallichi_.

### Valerian in Herbal Combinations

In addition to the effectiveness of valerian alone, 19 studies evaluated the effectiveness of valerian in combination with other herbs or other agents, among which 16 studies used _V. officinalis_,[65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323), [72](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr72-2515690X20967323), [82](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr82-2515690X20967323)– [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323), [88](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr88-2515690X20967323), [89](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr89-2515690X20967323), [73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323)– [80](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr80-2515690X20967323) 2 studies used _V. wallichii_,[81](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr81-2515690X20967323), [87](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr87-2515690X20967323) and 1 study used an unknown valerian species.[76](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr76-2515690X20967323) One study treated menopausal women with valerian essence in combination with lemon balm and observed sleep improvement, however the species and extraction methods were unidentified.[76](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr76-2515690X20967323)

Among 16 reports using herbal combinations with _V. officinals_, 8 studies examined the effects on sleep quality and/or latency and all those interventions led to positive outcomes.[65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323), [72](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr72-2515690X20967323), [75](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr75-2515690X20967323), [79](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr79-2515690X20967323), [83](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr83-2515690X20967323), [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323), [88](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr88-2515690X20967323), [89](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr89-2515690X20967323) Six studies evaluated anxiolytic potential, and all those studies found positive outcomes at least for one of the measures at one of the tested dosages[73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323), [77](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr77-2515690X20967323), [78](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr78-2515690X20967323), [85](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr85-2515690X20967323), [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323), [88](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr88-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 3-5\] and 3 observational studies). However, a study using the combination of _V. officinals_, _Passiflora incarnata_ (syn. _P. edulis_), and _Melissa officinalis_ extracts (single dose) found that the intervention attenuated anxiety under stress, although it did not alter the level of salivary cortisol, a physiological parameter of stress reactions[77](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr77-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 5\]). In another study, _V. officinalis_ and _M. officinalis_ combination (extract weight ratio 3:2) at 1,800 mg (single dose) increased anxiety while the same formulation at 600 mg reduced anxiety[78](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr78-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 3\]). Both of these negative outcomes were observed for single doses in healthy subjects. On the other hand, the other 4 studies, conducted with subjects with adjustment insomnia,[88](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr88-2515690X20967323) somatoform disorder patients[73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 4\]), depression patients[85](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr85-2515690X20967323) (observational), and children with affective disorders[86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) (observational), found that the herbal combinations with _V. officinalis_ were effective in reducing anxiety. Of note, when depression patients were treated with _V. officinalis_ (500 or 1,000 mg extract) and _Hypericum perforatum_ (600 mg extract) for 6 weeks, higher valerian dose (1,000 mg) reduced anxiety more effectively[85](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr85-2515690X20967323) (observational). In addition, a study found that a combination of _V. officinalis_ and _M. officinalis_ extracts was effective in reducing the symptoms in children with hyperactivity and concentration difficulties[84](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr84-2515690X20967323) (observational). In a study with Intensive Care Unit (ICU) patients, _V. officinalis_ essential oil combined with acupressure effectively induced relaxation and improved sleep[74](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr74-2515690X20967323) (observational). _V. wallichii_ with 8 ayurvedic herbs improved sleep in sleep onset insomnia patients[81](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr81-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 4\]), and _V. wallichii_ with milk improved sleep in primary insomnia patients[87](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr87-2515690X20967323) (observational).

With respect to the potential herbal partners of _V. officinalis_, _Humulus lupulus_ was the most frequently used in the clinical trials. All 7 reports that examined the effects on sleep or associated parameters observed sleep improvement[65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323), [72](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr72-2515690X20967323), [79](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr79-2515690X20967323), [83](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr83-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 2-3\]), EEG power alteration toward sleep[82](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr82-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 2\]), and reduced arousal[80](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr80-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 3\]) were observed. _M. officinalis_ used in 5 trials,[73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323), [77](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr77-2515690X20967323), [78](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr78-2515690X20967323), [84](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr84-2515690X20967323), [89](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr89-2515690X20967323) was the second most frequently combined herb, followed by _P. incarnata_ used in 4 trials.[73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323), [75](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr75-2515690X20967323), [77](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr77-2515690X20967323), [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) The 2 herbs were used in combination with _V. officinalis_ for sleep problems and anxiety, resulting in positive outcomes.[73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323), [75](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr75-2515690X20967323), [77](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr77-2515690X20967323), [78](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr78-2515690X20967323), [84](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr84-2515690X20967323), [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323), [89](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr89-2515690X20967323) Two studies were conducted on the combination of _V. officinalis_ and _H. perforatum_ with depression patients[85](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr85-2515690X20967323) (observational) and children with affective disorders[86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) (observational), and the intervention reduced anxiety,[85](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr85-2515690X20967323), [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) improved sleep,[86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) and reduced depression symptoms.[85](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr85-2515690X20967323) Two studies used _M. officinalis_ and _P. incarnata_ [73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323), [77](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr77-2515690X20967323) (RCTs \[Jadad scale 4-5\]), and 1 study used _H. lupulus_ and _P. incarnata_ [75](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr75-2515690X20967323) (RCT \[Jadad scale 4\]) in combination with _V. officinalis_. These 4 frequently used herbal partners and the study outcomes are summarized in [Figure 6](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig6-2515690X20967323). It was not possible to perform meta-analysis for herbal combinations due to the highly variable outcome measures.

![](https://journals.sagepub.com/cms/10.1177/2515690X20967323/asset/9f4261b1-2aca-46e6-af15-42f26535abb6/assets/images/large/10.1177_2515690x20967323-fig6.jpg)Figure 6. _V. officinalis_ and herbal partners. Frequently used herbal partners and potential uses supported by evidence are shown with number of studies and total number of subjects (n).

### Safety

There were no serious adverse events reported in the studies included in this review (60 studies, total n=6,894). Paradoxical stimulation,[16](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr16-2515690X20967323), [99](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr99-2515690X20967323) such as agitation and restlessness, was experienced only in minority.[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323), [78](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr78-2515690X20967323), [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) In older women with insomnia, valerian extract increased WASO,[53](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr53-2515690X20967323) suggesting it could have stimulatory effects. However, a study found that the same formulation at a higher dose increased anxiety while a lower dose was anxiolytic,[78](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr78-2515690X20967323) suggesting that paradoxical stimulation could be avoided by cautious dosing. Six studies investigated possible adverse effects on cognitive performance after _V. officinalis_ extract intake (single dose) in healthy adults[37](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr37-2515690X20967323), [39](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr39-2515690X20967323), [47](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr47-2515690X20967323), [49](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr49-2515690X20967323), [62](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr62-2515690X20967323) and elderly volunteers.[45](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr45-2515690X20967323) _V. officinalis_ standardized extracts at 100-1,600 mg did not impair cognitive or psychomotor performance[37](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr37-2515690X20967323), [39](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr39-2515690X20967323), [45](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr45-2515690X20967323), [47](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr47-2515690X20967323), [49](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr49-2515690X20967323), [62](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr62-2515690X20967323) and were proven safer compared to triazolam, temazepam (benzodiazepines), and diphenhydramine (antihistamine).[45](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr45-2515690X20967323), [47](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr47-2515690X20967323) Valerian did not cause any adverse events in postmenopausal women with insomnia,[57](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr57-2515690X20967323) older women with insomnia,[53](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr53-2515690X20967323) children with intellectual deficits and primary sleep problems,[46](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr46-2515690X20967323) and psychophysiological insomnia patients.[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323) Mild adverse events were reported in RLS patients (vivid dreams and fatigue),[30](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr30-2515690X20967323) arthritis patients with sleep disturbance (dizziness and sleepiness),[54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323) sleep-disturbed subjects (drowsiness),[50](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr50-2515690X20967323) insomnia patients (gastrointestinal symptoms),[42](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr42-2515690X20967323), [70](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr70-2515690X20967323) and outpatients with stress-induced insomnia (vivid dreams, drowsiness, heavy dream and depression),[66](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr66-2515690X20967323) however there was no clear association with the treatments. Potential herb-drug interaction was addressed by examining the effects on cytochrome p450 (CYP) expression levels, and no significant impact was detected at least for CYP1A2, CYP2D6, CYP2E1 and CYP3A4/5.[69](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr69-2515690X20967323), [68](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr68-2515690X20967323) As a whole, valerian is safe in all ages.

## Discussion

Concurring sleep problems and anxiety are frequently observed and their onset and course are interrelated.[100](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr100-2515690X20967323), [101](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr101-2515690X20967323) In addition, these disorders are associated with a number of comorbid conditions including depression,[101](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr101-2515690X20967323)– [103](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr103-2515690X20967323) dementia,[5](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr5-2515690X20967323), [6](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr6-2515690X20967323) OCD,[104](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr104-2515690X20967323) and hot flashes[105](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr105-2515690X20967323)– [107](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr107-2515690X20967323) ( [Figure 6](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig6-2515690X20967323)). Our results demonstrated that sleep promotion and anxiolytic effects were the major therapeutic benefits expected of valerian ( _V. officinalis_), and this herb could be also useful in treating OCD, cognitive dysfunction, menopausal hot flashes, as well as menstrual problems. However, the study outcomes considerably differed particularly when herbal extracts were used. We address this issue by discussing potential mechanisms underlying the therapeutic actions of valerian.

### Key Constituents and Mechanisms of Actions

Although the use of valerian extracts as a sedative and sleep aid dates back to the 18th century and a number of constituents have been identified in the last 120 years,[108](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr108-2515690X20967323) the active constituents and underlying mechanisms for the reported activities remain obscure.[109](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr109-2515690X20967323) The identified constituents include iridoids known as valepotriates (valtrate, isovaltrate, didrovaltrate and acevaltrate),[110](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr110-2515690X20967323) essential oil constituents including monoterpenes (e.g. borneol, bornyl acetate), sesquiterpenes (e.g. valerenal, valerenic acid), and carboxylic compounds (valeric / isovaleric acid),[111](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr111-2515690X20967323) lignans,[112](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr112-2515690X20967323) flavonoids,[108](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr108-2515690X20967323), [113](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr113-2515690X20967323) and low levels of γ-aminobutyric acid (GABA).[114](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr114-2515690X20967323) _Valeriana edulis_ (Mexican valerian) _Valeriana wallichii_ (Indian valerian) contain higher levels of iridoids, while valerenic acid and acetoxyvalerenic acid are unique to _V. officinalis._ [98](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr98-2515690X20967323)

### Valerian and GABAergic Signaling

GABA is an inhibitory neurotransmitter within the central nervous system and is a key target of pharmacotherapies in the treatment of anxiety and sleep disorders.[115](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr115-2515690X20967323), [116](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr116-2515690X20967323) GABA is present in the central nervous system (CNS), where it plays a role in the maintenance of balance between excitatory and inhibitory neurotransmissions. GABA acts via 3 subclasses of receptors termed GABAA, GABAB, and GABAC, each of which has distinct characteristics. GABAA and GABAC receptors are ligand-gated ion channels, while GABAB members are G-protein coupled receptors. GABAA receptors are heteropentameric transmembrane protein complexes made up of α1-6, β1-3, γ1-3, δ, ε, θ, π subunits, and have numerous allosteric binding sites.[116](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr116-2515690X20967323) Although it is not very likely that GABA in valerian, taken orally, directly exerts any therapeutic action, valerenic acid and valerenol can allosterically modulate GABAA receptors to enhance the response of GABAA to GABA _in vitro_,[117](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr117-2515690X20967323)– [119](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr119-2515690X20967323) and both valerenic acid and valerenol exerted anxiolytic activity in a GABAA β3 subunit-dependent manner in mice.[117](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr117-2515690X20967323) On the other hand, valerenic acid derivatives (e.g. acetoxy valerenic acid and hydroxy valerenic acid) bind the identical sites without inducing allosteric modulation, suggesting that these constituents can potentially compete with valerenic acid.[120](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr120-2515690X20967323) In fact, in an anxiety model in rodents, a valerian extract containing valerenic acid at a high level and acetoxy valerenic acid at a low level exhibited higher anxiolytic potency compared to an extract with acetoxy valerenic at a high level, indicating that standardization with respect to the total amount of valerenic acids (both valerenic acid and acetoxy valerenic acid) is inappropriate.[120](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr120-2515690X20967323) In addition, an aqueous extract of valerian induced GABA release in rat brain synaptosomes _in vitro_,[121](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr121-2515690X20967323) suggesting the presence of hydrophilic constituents potentially promotes GABAergic signaling. Expected mechanisms of actions are summarized in [Figure 5](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig5-2515690X20967323). Of note, the expression patterns of GABA receptors in humans are sex- and age-dependent, and GABAA β3 subunit levels in the superior temporal gyrus were lower in older women than old men,[122](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr122-2515690X20967323) suggesting that valerian’s actions via GABAergic signaling could depend on the sex and age.

### Valerian and Serotonergic Signaling

Serotonin (5-HT) plays essential roles in the regulation of sleep and mood, and serotonergic system is a promising therapeutic target for psychiatric disorders including anxiety, depression, and sleep disorders.[123](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr123-2515690X20967323)– [126](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr126-2515690X20967323) Both valerian extract and valerenic acid exhibit partial agonist activity at 5-HT receptor 5A (5-HT5A) _in vitro_,[127](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr127-2515690X20967323) suggesting the involvement of serotonergic system in the actions of valerian. There are 7 families of its receptors (5-HT1-7). Although the functional significance of 5-HT5A remains obscure, 5-HT5A is present at high levels in the regions that regulate circadian rhythms (the suprachiasmatic nucleus, the intergeniculate leaflet,[128](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr128-2515690X20967323), [129](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr129-2515690X20967323) the median raphe nuclei, and dorsal raphe nucleus) and colocalized with serotonin, suggesting the auto-receptor role of 5-HT5A in circadian regulation.[128](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr128-2515690X20967323) In addition, 5-HT5A is expressed in the brain areas such as the cerebral cortex, hippocampus, amygdala and hypothalamus,[129](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr129-2515690X20967323) suggesting that it is potentially involved in stress reactivity and resilience. Indeed, a study demonstrated that 5-HT5A antagonists could have different sedative, anxiolytic, and anti-depressant properties[130](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr130-2515690X20967323) ( [Figure 6](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig6-2515690X20967323)). These data suggest that valerian, as a 5-HT5A partial agonist, may act differently depending on what circumstances the subjects were placed and this could possibly explain the inconsistent outcomes among the trials.

### Valerian and Adenosine Signaling

Adenosine receptors play important roles in mood and anxiety disorders.[131](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr131-2515690X20967323) Adenosine A1 receptor activation reduces anxiety-like behavior in mice[132](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr132-2515690X20967323) and positive allosteric modulators of adenosine A1 receptor could be potential anxiolytic therapy.[133](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr133-2515690X20967323), [134](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr134-2515690X20967323) In addition, adenosine helps maintain brain homeostasis by preventing over excitation and regulating the sleep-wake rhythm.[135](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr135-2515690X20967323)– [137](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr137-2515690X20967323) Sleep stages are divided into 1 stage of rapid eye movement (REM) sleep and 4 stages of non-rapid eye movement (NREM) sleep (Stages 1-4) that are characterized by increasing sleep depth.[4](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr4-2515690X20967323), [138](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr138-2515690X20967323) The deeper stages (Stages 3 and 4) are believed to be the most restorative and collectively called SWS.[4](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr4-2515690X20967323), [138](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr138-2515690X20967323) Adenosine acting through A1 receptors facilitates sleep and increases slow wave activity (SWA) in SWS, whereas A1 receptor antagonism suppresses SWA.[139](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr139-2515690X20967323) Importantly, 2 studies found that _V. officinalis_ could increase SWS,[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323), [38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323) possibly contributing to the improved subjective sleep quality while objective sleep latency remained unchanged.[36](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr36-2515690X20967323) These observations suggest that valerian may promote the sleep quality by inducing deep sleep via adenosine A1 receptor signaling. In fact, a polar extract of valerian exhibited partial agonistic activity at A1 receptors[140](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr140-2515690X20967323) and valerian contains hydrophilic constituents that interact with adenosine signaling, such as lignans of a olivil derivatives that is a partial agonist of adenosine A1 receptors.[112](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr112-2515690X20967323), [141](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr141-2515690X20967323) Thus, valerian’s hydrophilic constituents could exert the anxiolytic and sleep-inducing effects via adenosine signaling. Importantly, while the hydrophilic extract was agonistic, isovaltrate in the hydrophobic extract acted as an inverse agonist at adenosine A1 receptor.[140](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr140-2515690X20967323) These findings indicate the hydrophilic and hydrophobic components of valerian act in opposite directions at adenosine receptors,[140](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr140-2515690X20967323) supporting the traditional use of water-based extract as a sleep aid,[16](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr16-2515690X20967323), [140](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr140-2515690X20967323) and possibly explaining the contradictory findings regarding the efficacy of valerian hydroalcoholic extracts.

### Valepotriates

Valepotriates are unstable thermolabile compounds that rapidly decompose. The characteristic odor of dried valerian is due to isovaleric acid released from decomposing valepotriates.[142](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr142-2515690X20967323) Although the mechanistic roles of valepotriates in the therapeutic effects are yet to be clarified, pre-clinical evidence suggests that valepotriates exert anxiolytic[143](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr143-2515690X20967323) and antidepressant-like effects,[144](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr144-2515690X20967323), [145](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr145-2515690X20967323) possibly via the dopaminergic and noradrenergic neurotransmission but not via the serotonergic system.[145](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr145-2515690X20967323) The monoaminergic neurotransmitters (dopamine, noradrenaline, and 5-HT) play overlapping roles in the etiology of anxiety and depression, and medications targeting these systems are proved to be effective in treating both anxiety and depression.[146](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr146-2515690X20967323) Moreover, those monoamines play a role in sleep-wake regulation.[147](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr147-2515690X20967323) Thus, the presence of valepotriates is likely to be essential in treating these disorders. In addition, valtrate reduced the serum glucocorticoid level in a rat anxiety model,[148](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr148-2515690X20967323) suggesting hypothalamus-pituitary-adrenal axis modulatory potential of valepotriates. Considering the significant association between neuroendocrine-immune axis imbalance and stress vulnerability and resilience,[149](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr149-2515690X20967323) the potential impact on the hypothalamus-pituitary-adrenal axis is particularly important. Stress can disturb the sleep, and stress reactivity is implicated in vulnerability to insomnia and other stress-related disorders such as anxiety and depression.[8](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr8-2515690X20967323), [150](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr150-2515690X20967323) Furthermore, glucocorticoid imbalance could lead to amyloid formation and tau accumulation, hallmarks of Alzheimer’s disease,[151](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr151-2515690X20967323) and elevated glucocorticoid levels are associated with neurodegenerative disorders.[152](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr152-2515690X20967323) Thus, valepotriates may prevent stress-induced neuropsychiatric disorders including anxiety and depression, as well as cognitive dysfunction, by restoring endocrine-immune balance. Expected mechanisms of action are summarized in [Figure 6](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig6-2515690X20967323).

### Quality and Shelf Life

As described above, multiple constituents, including valerenic acids, lignan, and valepotriates, differentially contribute to the therapeutic effectiveness of valerian. However, most of the commercially available valerian extracts are standardized to the levels of valerenic acids, while the contents of valepotriates are often unknown. Importantly, Bos et al. compared freshly prepared tincture (70% EtOH extract) and the same extract stored at room temperature for 2 months, and found that the levels of valepotriates (valtrate and isovaltrate) after 2 months were less than 5% of the original, whereas the levels of valerenic acids (valerenic acid and acetoxyvalerenic acid) were not affected.[98](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr98-2515690X20967323) This finding suggests that the shelf life of valerian extracts may be significantly shorter if the levels of valepotriates are considered. It is possible that the negative outcomes observed in the trials using valerian extracts, rather than the raw materials, could have been caused by the loss of valepotriates in those extracts.

In the United States, valerian-containing products are widely available as dietary supplements, in various forms under various trade names. Examples are Valerian (NOW FOODS, IL, US; Nature’s Way, WI, USA), Standardized Valerian (root extract standardized to 0.8% valerenic acids; Nature’s Way), and Amantilla (hydroalcoholic extract; NutraMedix, FL, USA), to name a few. In Europe, the Committee on Herbal Medicine Products (HMPC) concluded that valerian-containing medicinal products have to be assessed by the responsible national authorities. Available products include Baldrian (85% ethanol extract; Kneipp, Würzburg, Germany), and Baldrianwurzel (70% ethanol extract; Hofapotheke St. Afra, Augsburg, Germany). Herbal combinations are also available (e.g. Valeirana-Melissa extract \[standardized to 0.8% valerenic acids; Bonusan, Rotterdam, Netherlands\]). Of note, the recommended storage temperatures for most of these products are at or below room temperature (around 25°C).

### Limitation

The current study has reviewed the effectiveness of valerian without specifying target populations. This raises a limitation as the etiology underlying sleep problems and associated health problems could be diverse depending on age, sex, and general health conditions. Consequently, there could be potential differences in the outcomes depending on the target populations, however such possibilities were not addressed in this review. In addition, heterogeneity in the outcome measures limited the number of data sources for meta-analysis, which in turn limits the generalizability of the results. Further research is needed to assess the effectiveness for specific populations and outcomes.

### Conclusion

According to the 1905 edition of King’s American dispensatory,[99](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr99-2515690X20967323) ‘valerian excites the cerebro-spinal system.’ and ‘in medicinal doses it acts as a stimulant-tonic,…’, which suggests that valerian is not a simple hypnotic or anxiolytic agent. In addition, the text continues that ‘The extract of valerian is worthless, but the fluid extract has been found to possess all the medicinal virtues of the root’,[99](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr99-2515690X20967323) suggesting that extraction methods could play a crucial role in preserving the therapeutic potency. Valerian has diverse chemical properties. As summarized in [Table 3](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#table3-2515690X20967323), the differences in polarity can lead to variability in the quality of valerian extracts depending on the extraction solvents. Our study has found that the hydroalcoholic extracts used in the clinical trials are variable with respect to the solvents ( [Table 4](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#table4-2515690X20967323)), and their phytochemical properties are not characterized in most cases. Furthermore, there is no information regarding the storage conditions such as temperature and storage period. Considering the low stability of some of the important active constituents,[98](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr98-2515690X20967323), [142](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr142-2515690X20967323) it is unknown to what extent the active constituents had been preserved at the end of those trials. The absence of such information limits the discussion as to why some extracts were ineffective while others exhibited effectiveness in those clinical trials. Due to the multiple active constituents and complex mechanisms of actions ( [Figure 5](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#fig5-2515690X20967323)), it is imperative to use well characterized plant materials and extracts in the future clinical trials, in order for the evaluation of valerian’s true effectiveness to be possible.

|  | Extraction solvent | References |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 70% Ethanol | Roh D, 2019[34](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr34-2515690X20967323); Hallam KT, 2003[47](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr47-2515690X20967323); Taibi DM, 2009[54](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr54-2515690X20967323); Taibi DM, 2009[53](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr53-2515690X20967323); Diaper A, 2004[50](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr50-2515690X20967323); Donovan JL, 2004[69](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr69-2515690X20967323); Ziegler G, 2002[44](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr44-2515690X20967323) |
| 2 | 45% Methanol | Meier S, 2018[77](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr77-2515690X20967323); Melzer J, 2009[73](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr73-2515690X20967323); Koetter U, 2007[65](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr65-2515690X20967323); Morin CM, 2005[79](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr79-2515690X20967323); Schellenberg R, 2004[80](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr80-2515690X20967323); Vonderheid-Guth B, 2000[82](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr82-2515690X20967323) |
| 3 | 62% Ethanol | Gromball J, 2014[84](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr84-2515690X20967323); Müller SF, 2006[89](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr89-2515690X20967323) |
| 4 | 60% Ethanol | Oxman AD, 2007[46](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr46-2515690X20967323) |
| 5 | 40% Ethanol | Trompetter I, 2013[86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) |

This study demonstrated that valerian could be a safe and useful herb alone and also in combination in treating sleep problems, anxiety, and associated comorbidities. One possibility for exploration that arises is whether valerian is particularly useful in treating insomnia where there are higher levels of anxiety. In fact, the observation that _V. edulis_ reduced sleep problems most effectively in children with hyperactivity[46](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr46-2515690X20967323) may suggest that valerian is more useful in treating insomnia associated with particular psychiatric conditions such as anxiety. The safety has been proven in a wide range from childhood[46](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr46-2515690X20967323), [84](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr84-2515690X20967323), [86](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr86-2515690X20967323) to old age.[38](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr38-2515690X20967323), [45](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr45-2515690X20967323), [53](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr53-2515690X20967323) Sleep problems are associated with a number of comorbidities including anxiety, depression, and dementia in both adulthood[123](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr123-2515690X20967323), [153](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr153-2515690X20967323) and childhood.[154](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr154-2515690X20967323) As we age, the quantity and quality of sleep decrease,[155](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr155-2515690X20967323), [156](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr156-2515690X20967323) and insomnia and daytime drowsiness are frequently reported in the older population.[157](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/2515690X20967323#bibr157-2515690X20967323) Thus, valerian may help improve the quality of life in all ages by improving sleep quality, thereby preventing a number of psychiatric and cognitive dysfunctions. However, due to the presence of multiple active constituents and the unstable nature of some components, it may be useful to revise the standardization methods and shelf life of the extracts. Repeated treatments with the whole root / rhizome consistently promoted sleep quality at 450-1410 mg per day for 4-8 weeks, whereas valerian extracts 300-600 mg per day for 5 days-4 weeks resulted in inconsistent outcomes. Evidence is poor with respect to the effectiveness of single dose intervention as a sleep aid. Developing effective standardization methods would be desirable. Meanwhile, the usage of whole herbal substances (root / rhizome), rather than extracts, may be the way to obtain optimal efficacy for the time being.

Lastly, due to the subjective nature of sleep problems and associated mood disorders, there remains a difficulty in determining the best measure for the efficacy of interventions. The ultimate goal of any therapies, whether it be traditional, conventional or integrative, beyond disease ‘cure’ or modulation, is to improve the quality of life for patients. While objective measures in a laboratory setting provide valuable information and mechanistic understanding, it may be useful to consider additional and more important factors that need to be addressed specifically in each individual. Such measures and tailor-made approaches would necessarily involve sufficient interaction and communication between patients and practitioners. Developing effective trial strategies to address this issue is a future challenge.
